
# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS, enabling authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, thereby streamlining financial management and enhancing data security for customers.

# Functional Flows

1. Journey Name: User Authentication and Dashboard Access  
   Functionality: Users authenticate through Cognito to access their personalized dashboard.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: The React-based web app is served via Amazon CloudFront, ensuring global delivery with caching.  
   - **Authentication & Authorization**: Users authenticate using Amazon Cognito User Pool, which supports MFA for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the app obtains IdToken and AccessToken.  
   - **Backend**: The app calls the API Gateway, which validates the JWT token using Cognito Authorizer, and forwards the request to AWS Lambda.  
   - **Data Layer**: Lambda interacts with DynamoDB to fetch and display user-specific transaction metadata on the dashboard.  

2. Journey Name: Transaction Processing  
   Functionality: Processes user transactions and updates the database with transaction metadata.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Backend**: API Gateway receives transaction requests and forwards them to AWS Lambda.  
   - **Data Layer**: Lambda writes transaction metadata to DynamoDB, using merchantId as the partition key and transactionTimestamp as the sort key.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker that normalizes the data and writes aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for financial reporting.  

3. Journey Name: Financial Report Generation  
   Functionality: Generates and delivers monthly financial reports to users.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: Users request a "monthly report" via the web app.  
   - **Backend**: API Gateway forwards the request to AWS Lambda, which initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: Step Functions manage the multi-step process of aggregating data from Aurora.  
   - **Data Layer**: The final report is stored in an S3 private bucket, ensuring confidentiality and secure access.  

4. Journey Name: Security and Observability  
   Functionality: Ensures secure operations and monitors system health.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Security Controls**: Implements encryption for S3, DynamoDB, and Aurora using KMS-managed keys, and enforces TLS 1.2 for secure data transmission.  
   - **IAM Controls**: Utilizes least privilege roles and avoids wildcard actions to minimize security risks.  
   - **Observability**: Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses, while AWS X-Ray provides request tracing for performance insights.  

5. Journey Name: Networking and Data Security  
   Functionality: Manages secure network configurations and data protection.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Networking**: Utilizes VPC with private subnets for Aurora and Lambdas, and public subnets for NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are used for DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager to ensure secure data access.  
   - **Data Security**: AWS Secrets Manager manages database passwords and API secrets, ensuring they are securely stored and accessed.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: Amazon CloudFront
   - Purpose of integration: Delivers the web application globally with caching
   - Type of integration: CDN
   - Authentication method used: None specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Static web content (HTML, JS, CSS)

2. Name of the third-party service: Amazon Cognito
   - Purpose of integration: User authentication and authorization
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: Token-based authentication (ID, Access tokens)
   - Data shared with the third party: User authentication data

3. Name of the third-party service: Amazon API Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Serves as the entry point for API requests
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: Cognito JWT validation
   - Data shared with the third party: API requests and responses

4. Name of the third-party service: AWS Lambda
   - Purpose of integration: Executes backend logic and processing
   - Type of integration: Function as a Service (FaaS)
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data, processing logic

5. Name of the third-party service: Amazon DynamoDB
   - Purpose of integration: Stores transaction metadata
   - Type of integration: Database
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction metadata

6. Name of the third-party service: Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 (PostgreSQL)
   - Purpose of integration: Stores financial reporting and aggregated data
   - Type of integration: Database
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Financial reporting data

7. Name of the third-party service: AWS Secrets Manager
   - Purpose of integration: Manages database passwords and API secrets
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Database passwords, API secrets

8. Name of the third-party service: Amazon SQS
   - Purpose of integration: Receives event notifications from the backend
   - Type of integration: Messaging queue
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Event notifications

9. Name of the third-party service: AWS Step Functions
   - Purpose of integration: Manages multi-step reporting workflows
   - Type of integration: Workflow service
   - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
   - Data shared with the third party: Workflow execution data

10. Name of the third-party service: Amazon CloudWatch
    - Purpose of integration: Provides logging and monitoring
    - Type of integration: Monitoring service
    - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
    - Data shared with the third party: Logs, metrics, alarms

11. Name of the third-party service: AWS X-Ray
    - Purpose of integration: Provides request tracing
    - Type of integration: Tracing service
    - Authentication method used: AWS IAM roles
    - Data shared with the third party: Request tracing data

12. Name of the third-party service: Amazon Route 53
    - Purpose of integration: Handles DNS
    - Type of integration: DNS service
    - Authentication method used: None specified
    - Data shared with the third party: DNS records

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It provides the user interface for interacting with the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static site, consisting of HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, is hosted on Amazon S3. Amazon CloudFront is used to deliver the web application globally with caching capabilities to enhance performance and reduce latency.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice itself does not process or store data. It serves static content and interacts with backend services to fetch and display data to the user. Any data processing or storage is handled by the backend services.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static files for the React application.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally and caches content for improved performance.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the application, ensuring users can access the web app via a domain name.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used to access backend services securely.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and bots by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Encryption**: Data in transit is protected using TLS 1.2.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized services and users can access the resources needed by the Frontend microservice.

## Server Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. It is served as static files (HTML, JS, CSS) hosted on Amazon S3.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The frontend processes user interaction data and displays transaction and financial report data retrieved from the backend. It does not store any sensitive data locally, as it relies on backend services for data retrieval and processing.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - Amazon CloudFront: Delivers the web application globally with caching to improve performance and reduce latency.
   - Amazon Route 53: Handles DNS routing for the frontend application.
   - AWS WAF: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web attacks.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The frontend integrates with Amazon Cognito for user authentication. It supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP to enhance security.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - AWS WAF is used to protect against automated bot attacks and other web-based threats.
   - The frontend is served over HTTPS, ensuring that all data in transit is encrypted using TLS 1.2.
   - The S3 bucket hosting the static site is configured with encryption (AES-256) to protect data at rest.
   - The frontend application does not expose any public S3 buckets, adhering to best practices for data security.

## File System Microservice

1. **Primary Functionality and Purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical Stack and Frameworks Used**  
   - **React**: The web application is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces, particularly single-page applications.
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React site, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: A content delivery network (CDN) that globally delivers the web application with caching to improve load times and reduce latency.

3. **Data Processed and Stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily handles static assets and does not process or store user data directly. It serves the static files necessary for the client-side application to function.

4. **Integration Points with Other Services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Integrates with Amazon S3 to deliver the static assets globally.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web application attacks.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS routing for the web application, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.

5. **Authentication Mechanisms**  
   While the Frontend microservice itself does not handle authentication, it relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used by the client application to interact with backend services securely.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by filtering malicious traffic and preventing attacks such as SQL injection and cross-site scripting (XSS).
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure communication between users and the web application.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized services and users can access the S3 bucket hosting the static assets, adhering to the principle of least privilege.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS managed services to ensure scalability, security, and global accessibility.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is handled by Amazon Cognito, where the user is verified through a secure login process with multi-factor authentication enabled. Upon successful authentication, the application retrieves an IdToken and AccessToken, which are used to securely call the backend API hosted on Amazon API Gateway. The API Gateway, protected by AWS WAF, routes the request to AWS Lambda functions, which interact with Amazon DynamoDB to fetch and display the user's transaction data on the dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and forwards it to a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB, ensuring data integrity and confidentiality. DynamoDB Streams trigger another Lambda worker function that normalizes the transaction data and writes aggregated information to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for financial reporting purposes. This flow ensures real-time processing and storage of transaction data, maintaining high availability and scalability.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the dashboard. This request is processed by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function to initiate an AWS Step Functions workflow. The workflow orchestrates multiple steps to aggregate data from Amazon Aurora, ensuring that the report is comprehensive and accurate. The final report is securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, encrypted with AES-256, and made available for the user to download. This flow provides users with timely and secure access to their financial reports, supporting informed decision-making.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which acts as a decoupling mechanism to ensure reliable message delivery. A dedicated Lambda worker function processes these events, normalizing the data and writing it to both DynamoDB and Aurora. This ensures that all incoming data is consistently processed and stored, supporting the system's data integrity and availability.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of system performance and identification of bottlenecks. This comprehensive monitoring setup ensures that the system remains reliable and any issues are promptly addressed.

6. **Security and Compliance**: The system employs robust security controls, including encryption of data at rest and in transit, IAM roles with least privilege access, and no public S3 buckets. AWS Secrets Manager manages database passwords and API secrets, ensuring that sensitive information is securely stored and accessed. These measures ensure compliance with data protection regulations and safeguard against unauthorized access and data breaches.

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend microservice utilizes a React-based web application, which is a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces, particularly single-page applications. The static assets of the application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice does not directly process or store sensitive data. Instead, it interacts with backend services to display transaction metadata, user profile information, and financial reports to authenticated users. The data displayed is fetched from backend services and is not stored on the client-side beyond session data necessary for user interaction.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: The web application is delivered globally through Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and improves the performance and availability of the application.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the web application, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by filtering malicious traffic using OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used to access backend services securely. Multi-factor authentication (MFA) is enabled, offering an additional layer of security through SMS or TOTP.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and bots by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Amazon S3 bucket encryption**: Ensures that static assets are encrypted using AES-256.
   - **TLS 1.2 enforced**: Ensures secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **No public S3 buckets**: Ensures that static assets are not publicly accessible, reducing the risk of unauthorized access.

## Server Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:  
   The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to interact with the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It provides users with the ability to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**:  
   The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static assets of the web application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**:  
   The frontend does not process or store sensitive data directly. It serves static content and interacts with backend services to display transaction data, user profiles, and financial reports to authenticated users.

4. **Integration points with other services**:  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: The web application is delivered globally through Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and improves access speed for users worldwide.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the web application, ensuring users can access the service via a user-friendly domain name.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web threats.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**:  
   The frontend relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication. Users authenticate through Cognito User Pools, which supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP. Once authenticated, users receive ID and Access tokens to interact with the backend services securely.

6. **Security controls implemented**:  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against web exploits and bots by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **S3 bucket encryption**: Ensures that static assets are encrypted at rest using AES-256.
   - **TLS 1.2 enforced**: Ensures secure communication between the client and the server.
   - **No public S3 buckets**: Ensures that the S3 buckets hosting the static assets are not publicly accessible, reducing the risk of unauthorized access.

1. **Primary Functionality and Purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the 'Frontend' microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a globally accessible and responsive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical Stack and Frameworks Used**

   The frontend microservice primarily processes user interaction data and requests for authentication and API calls. It does not store any sensitive data locally but interacts with backend services to fetch and display data.

   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Integrates with Amazon S3 to deliver static assets and with AWS WAF for security.

   - **Amazon Cognito**: Manages user authentication and authorization. It provides token-based authentication using ID and Access tokens, with Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) enabled for enhanced security.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and bots by using OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Provides additional security by caching content and reducing the attack surface.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized users and services have access to the frontend resources, adhering to the principle of least privilege.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. Journey Name: User Authentication and Dashboard Access  
   Functionality: Authenticated users access their personalized dashboard to view transactions and reconcile payments.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: The user accesses the React-based web app hosted on Amazon S3, delivered globally via Amazon CloudFront.  
   - **Authentication & Authorization**: Amazon Cognito User Pool authenticates the user with MFA enabled, providing IdToken and AccessToken.  
   - **Backend**: The app calls Amazon API Gateway, which validates the Cognito JWT and routes the request to AWS Lambda.  
   - **Data Layer**: AWS Lambda retrieves transaction metadata from Amazon DynamoDB using IAM roles with least privilege.  

2. Journey Name: Transaction Processing  
   Functionality: Processing and storing transaction data securely and efficiently.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Backend**: API Gateway receives transaction data and invokes AWS Lambda.  
   - **Data Layer**: Lambda writes transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB, ensuring data is encrypted with KMS-managed keys.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker to process the data further.  
   - **Data Layer**: The worker writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2, encrypted with KMS CMK keys.  

3. Journey Name: Financial Report Generation  
   Functionality: Generating and delivering monthly financial reports to users.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: Users request a monthly report via the web app.  
   - **Backend**: API Gateway routes the request to AWS Lambda, which initiates AWS Step Functions.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: Step Functions manage the multi-step workflow to aggregate data from Aurora.  
   - **Data Layer**: The final report is stored in an S3 private bucket, ensuring confidentiality with AES-256 encryption.  

4. Journey Name: Event Notification and Processing  
   Functionality: Handling event notifications and processing them for data insights.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: Amazon SQS receives event notifications from the backend.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: AWS Lambda (Worker) normalizes incoming events and writes them to DynamoDB and Aurora for further analysis.  

5. Journey Name: Security and Observability  
   Functionality: Ensuring system security and monitoring for operational insights.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Security Controls**: Implement encryption across S3, DynamoDB, and Aurora, enforce TLS 1.2, and apply IAM controls with least privilege.  
   - **Observability**: Use Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms to monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses, and AWS X-Ray for request tracing.  

These functional flows provide a comprehensive overview of the system's operations, ensuring secure and efficient handling of user data and transactions.

   - **IAM Controls**: Implements least privilege access for any AWS resources the frontend may interact with indirectly through backend services.
   - **No public S3 buckets**: Ensures that the S3 bucket hosting the static site is not publicly accessible, reducing the risk of unauthorized access.

## Server Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:  
   The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to interact with the application, view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**:  
   The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static site, consisting of HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, is hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**:  
   The frontend processes user interactions and displays data retrieved from the backend services. It does not store any sensitive data locally, as it relies on backend services for data retrieval and processing.

4. **Integration points with other services**:  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally with caching to improve performance and reduce latency.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the application.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web threats.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**:  
   The frontend integrates with Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. It supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP to enhance security. Upon successful authentication, the frontend obtains ID and Access tokens to interact with backend APIs securely.

6. **Security controls implemented**:  
   - **AWS WAF**: Provides protection against common web exploits and automated bot attacks.
   - **Encryption**: S3 bucket encryption using AES-256 ensures that the static site files are stored securely.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.

## File System Microservice

1. **Primary Functionality and Purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the 'Frontend' microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a globally accessible and responsive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical Stack and Frameworks Used**  
   - **React**: The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces, particularly single-page applications.
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React site, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: A content delivery network (CDN) that delivers the web application globally with caching to improve load times and reduce latency.

3. **Data Processed and Stored**  
   The frontend microservice primarily handles static content delivery and does not process or store user data directly. However, it interacts with backend services to display transaction data, financial reports, and user-specific information.

4. **Integration Points with Other Services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Integrates with Amazon S3 to deliver static content efficiently.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web application attacks.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS routing for the frontend application, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.

5. **Authentication Mechanisms**  
   The frontend microservice relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used to authorize API requests to the backend services.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Web Application Firewall rules are applied to protect against common vulnerabilities and threats, such as SQL injection and cross-site scripting (XSS).
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **No Public S3 Buckets**: Ensures that static assets are not publicly accessible without going through CloudFront, reducing the risk of unauthorized access.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS, designed to enable authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, thereby enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is handled by Amazon Cognito, where the user is verified and provided with an IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are used by the application to securely call the backend API through Amazon API Gateway, which then triggers AWS Lambda functions to interact with Amazon DynamoDB, retrieving and displaying transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and invokes a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function that normalizes the data and writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. This ensures that transaction data is processed efficiently and stored securely for further analysis.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request financial reports, such as a monthly report, through the application. The request is routed via API Gateway to a Lambda function, which initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow. This workflow orchestrates the aggregation of data from Amazon Aurora, processes it, and stores the final report in a private Amazon S3 bucket. This flow ensures that financial reports are generated accurately and securely, maintaining data confidentiality and integrity.

4. **Data Ingestion & Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which queues the events for processing. A dedicated AWS Lambda worker function retrieves these events, normalizes them, and writes the processed data to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora. This flow ensures that data ingestion is handled efficiently, supporting real-time processing and storage.

5. **Observability & Monitoring**: The system's observability is managed through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, enabling detailed analysis of system performance and troubleshooting. This flow ensures that the system is monitored effectively, allowing for quick detection and resolution of issues.

6. **Security Controls & Data Protection**: The application employs multiple security controls, including encryption of S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora data using KMS-managed keys, and enforcing TLS 1.2 for data in transit. IAM roles are configured with least privilege, and no public S3 buckets are allowed. This flow ensures that data is protected against unauthorized access and potential breaches, maintaining compliance with data protection standards.

    - Data shared with the third party: Request tracing data

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for users to interact with the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend microservice utilizes a React-based web application, which is a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces, particularly single-page applications. The static assets of the application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice does not directly process or store data. Instead, it serves static content and interacts with backend services to fetch and display data to the user. The data displayed includes transaction metadata, user profile information, and financial reports, which are processed and stored by backend services.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: The web application is delivered globally through Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and improves the performance and availability of the application.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the application, ensuring users can access the web application via a user-friendly domain name.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web exploits and attacks.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens that the application uses to authorize API requests to the backend services.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by filtering and monitoring HTTP requests based on predefined security rules.
   - **Encryption**: Static assets stored in Amazon S3 are encrypted using AES-256 encryption.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized users and services have access to the necessary resources, following the principle of least privilege.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.

## Server Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to interact with the application, view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static assets of the React application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The frontend does not store data itself but processes user interactions and displays data retrieved from the backend services. It handles user authentication tokens and session data to maintain user state.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - The frontend integrates with Amazon CloudFront for global content delivery and caching, ensuring fast and reliable access to the application.
   - It interacts with Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization, obtaining ID and Access tokens for secure API calls.
   - The frontend communicates with the backend serverless API through Amazon API Gateway to fetch and display transaction data and reports.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - User authentication is managed through Amazon Cognito User Pool, which supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP. The frontend obtains ID and Access tokens from Cognito after successful user authentication.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - Amazon CloudFront is protected by AWS WAF, which uses OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate automated bot attacks and other threats.
   - The S3 bucket hosting the static site is encrypted with AES-256 to ensure data security.
   - TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing a secure platform to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services for enhanced performance and security.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is managed through Amazon Cognito, where the user is authenticated using multi-factor authentication (MFA) for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the application obtains an IdToken and AccessToken, which are used to securely call the backend APIs through Amazon API Gateway. The API Gateway, protected by AWS WAF, routes the request to AWS Lambda functions, which interact with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and forwards it to a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which normalizes the transaction data and writes aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. This ensures that all transaction data is securely processed and stored, maintaining data integrity and confidentiality.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request financial reports, such as a "monthly report," through the application. The request is handled by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function to initiate a multi-step workflow managed by AWS Step Functions. Step Functions orchestrate the aggregation of data from Amazon Aurora, ensuring that the report is comprehensive and accurate. The final report is securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, encrypted with AES-256, ensuring that sensitive financial data remains confidential.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which acts as a message queue to decouple the components of the application. AWS Lambda functions process these events, normalizing the data and writing it to both DynamoDB and Aurora. This ensures that the data pipeline is efficient and scalable, capable of handling high volumes of transactions without compromising performance.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of the application's performance and quick identification of any issues. This comprehensive monitoring setup ensures that the application remains reliable and any potential disruptions are promptly addressed.

6. **Security and Compliance**: The application employs robust security controls, including encryption of data at rest and in transit, least privilege IAM roles, and no public S3 buckets. AWS Secrets Manager manages database passwords and API secrets, ensuring that sensitive information is securely stored and accessed. These measures, combined with data classification and business risk assessments, ensure that the application complies with industry standards and protects against unauthorized access and data breaches.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS, designed to enable authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. User Authentication and Dashboard Access: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is managed by Amazon Cognito, where users are verified using multi-factor authentication (MFA) for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the application retrieves an IdToken and AccessToken, allowing the user to securely access the dashboard. The application then communicates with the backend through Amazon API Gateway, which routes requests to AWS Lambda functions. This workflow manages the multi-step process of aggregating data from Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. 4. Data Ingestion and Processing: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which queues the events for processing. An AWS Lambda worker function normalizes these incoming events and writes the processed data to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. 5. Observability and Monitoring: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of system performance and identification of potential bottlenecks or issues. This comprehensive monitoring setup ensures that the system remains reliable and any issues are promptly addressed.

6. Security Controls and Data Protection: The system employs robust security controls, including encryption of data at rest and in transit using KMS-managed keys and TLS 1.2. IAM roles are configured with the principle of least privilege, ensuring that access to resources is tightly controlled. Public S3 buckets are avoided, and all sensitive data, such as PCI-related transaction metadata and financial reports, are classified and protected according to their confidentiality level. This ensures that the system complies with security best practices and protects against unauthorized access and data breaches.

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless and responsive user interface globally.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static site, consisting of HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, is hosted on Amazon S3. Amazon CloudFront is used to deliver the web application globally, providing caching and reducing latency for users.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily processes user interface data, including transaction views, payment reconciliation interfaces, and financial report displays. It does not store sensitive data locally but interacts with backend services to fetch and display data as needed.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static files for the React application.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally with caching capabilities.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the application, ensuring users can access the service via a friendly domain name.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens. These tokens are used to authorize API calls to the backend services.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and bots by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Encryption**: Ensures data in transit is encrypted using TLS 1.2.
   - **IAM Controls**: Implements least privilege access for any AWS resources the Frontend might interact with, ensuring no wildcard actions and no public S3 buckets.

## Server Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. It is served as static files (HTML, JS, CSS) hosted on Amazon S3.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The frontend does not process or store data directly. It serves static content and interacts with backend services to display dynamic data to users.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - Amazon CloudFront: Delivers the web application globally with caching to improve performance and reduce latency.
   - Amazon Route 53: Handles DNS routing for the frontend application.
   - AWS WAF: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web vulnerabilities and attacks.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The frontend integrates with Amazon Cognito for user authentication. It supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP to enhance security.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - AWS WAF is used to protect the application from web exploits and attacks by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - Amazon CloudFront provides secure content delivery with caching, reducing the attack surface.
   - TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.

## File System Microservice

1. **Primary Functionality and Purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to provide a user-friendly interface for interacting with the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical Stack and Frameworks Used**  
   - **React**: The web application is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces.
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React site, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: A content delivery network (CDN) that delivers the web application globally with caching to improve performance and reduce latency.

3. **Data Processed and Stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily handles static content delivery and does not process or store dynamic data. It serves static files to users' browsers and interacts with backend services for dynamic data retrieval and processing.

4. **Integration Points with Other Services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Integrates with Amazon S3 to deliver static content globally.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web application attacks.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the web application, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.

5. **Authentication Mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice itself does not handle authentication directly but relies on integration with Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate via Cognito, which provides tokens that the frontend uses to access backend services securely.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application from common web exploits by filtering and monitoring HTTP requests.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Provides additional security features such as DDoS protection and secure delivery of content.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized users and services can access the frontend resources, adhering to the principle of least privilege.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS managed services to ensure scalability, security, and global accessibility.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user authentication process is initiated when a user opens the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, which ensures secure user login with MFA enabled. Once authenticated, the application obtains an IdToken and AccessToken, allowing the user to access the dashboard. The app then calls the API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda functions. These functions interact with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and triggers an AWS Lambda function. This function writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker, which processes the transaction data further. The worker normalizes the data and writes aggregated information to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2, ensuring that financial reporting data is up-to-date and securely stored.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request financial reports, such as a monthly report, through the application. This request is processed by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. The function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow that aggregates the necessary data from Amazon Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring that only authorized users can access the highly confidential financial reports.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. AWS Lambda workers then process these events, normalizing the data and writing it to both Amazon DynamoDB and Aurora. This ensures that all transaction and reporting data is consistently updated and available for analysis.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of system performance and potential bottlenecks.

6. **Security and Compliance**: The system employs multiple security controls, including encryption of data at rest and in transit, IAM roles with least privilege, and AWS WAF rules to protect against common web vulnerabilities. Data classification ensures that PCI-related transaction metadata, user profile information, and financial reports are handled according to their confidentiality requirements, mitigating business risks such as unauthorized access and data leakage.

# Third Party Integrations

1. **Amazon CloudFront**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Delivers the web application globally with caching.
   - **Type of integration:** CDN (Content Delivery Network)
   - **Authentication method used:** None (publicly accessible)
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Static web content (HTML, JS, CSS)

2. **Amazon Cognito**
   - **Purpose of integration:** User authentication and authorization.
   - **Type of integration:** API
   - **Authentication method used:** Token-based authentication (ID, Access tokens)
   - **Data shared with the third party:** User authentication data (IdToken, AccessToken)

3. **Amazon API Gateway**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Serves as the entry point for API requests.
   - **Type of integration:** API
   - **Authentication method used:** Cognito JWT validation
   - **Data shared with the third party:** API requests and responses

4. **Amazon S3**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Hosts static React site and stores financial reports.
   - **Type of integration:** Storage service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Static site content and financial report data

5. **Amazon DynamoDB**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Stores transaction metadata.
   - **Type of integration:** Database service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Transaction metadata

6. **Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 (PostgreSQL)**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Stores financial reporting and aggregated data.
   - **Type of integration:** Database service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Financial reporting and aggregated data

7. **AWS Secrets Manager**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Manages database passwords and API secrets.
   - **Type of integration:** Secret management service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Database passwords and API secrets

8. **Amazon SQS**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Receives event notifications from the backend.
   - **Type of integration:** Messaging service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Event notifications

9. **AWS Step Functions**
   - **Purpose of integration:** Manages multi-step reporting workflows.
   - **Type of integration:** Workflow orchestration service
   - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
   - **Data shared with the third party:** Workflow execution data

10. **Amazon CloudWatch**
    - **Purpose of integration:** Provides logging and monitoring.
    - **Type of integration:** Monitoring service
    - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
    - **Data shared with the third party:** Logs and monitoring data

11. **AWS X-Ray**
    - **Purpose of integration:** Provides request tracing.
    - **Type of integration:** Tracing service
    - **Authentication method used:** IAM roles and policies
    - **Data shared with the third party:** Request tracing data

These integrations are all part of the AWS ecosystem, which is considered a third-party service provider in this context.

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:  
   The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard web application. It allows authenticated users to interact with the system to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**:  
   The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. It is served globally via Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and content delivery capabilities.

3. **Data processed and stored**:  
   The frontend processes user interaction data and authentication tokens (IdToken and AccessToken) obtained from Amazon Cognito. It does not store any data persistently as it is a static site hosted on Amazon S3.

4. **Integration points with other services**:  
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static files (HTML, JS, CSS) for the React application.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally with caching.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the application.
   - **Amazon Cognito**: Handles user authentication and authorization.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**:  
   The frontend uses Amazon Cognito for user authentication. It supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) via SMS or TOTP and uses token-based authentication with ID and Access tokens.

6. **Security controls implemented**:  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects CloudFront with OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web vulnerabilities and attacks.
   - **Encryption**: TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures least privilege access and no wildcard actions for roles associated with the frontend service.

## Server Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:  
   The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to interact with the application, view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

   The frontend itself does not process or store sensitive data. It primarily serves static content and interacts with backend services to display dynamic data to the user.

6. **Security controls implemented**:  
   - **AWS WAF**: Implements OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to protect against common web vulnerabilities and automated attacks.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Ensures secure communication between the client and the server.
   - **Amazon S3 bucket encryption**: Uses AES-256 encryption to secure static assets stored in S3.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS, designed to enable authenticated users to efficiently view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, thereby enhancing financial management and decision-making for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. Journey Name: User Authentication and Dashboard Access  
   Functionality: Users authenticate via Cognito to access their personalized dashboard.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: The React-based web app is served via Amazon CloudFront, ensuring global delivery with caching.  
   - **Authentication & Authorization**: Users authenticate using Amazon Cognito User Pool, which supports MFA for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the app obtains IdToken and AccessToken.  
   - **Backend**: The app calls the Amazon API Gateway, which validates the JWT token using Cognito. The request is then processed by AWS Lambda functions, which interact with Amazon DynamoDB to fetch user-specific transaction metadata.  
   - **Data Layer**: DynamoDB stores transaction metadata, ensuring quick access and retrieval based on the partition key (merchantId) and sort key (transactionTimestamp).  
   - **Networking**: The VPC ensures secure communication between services, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambdas, and public subnets for the NAT gateway.  

2. Journey Name: Transaction Processing  
   Functionality: Processing and storing transaction data securely and efficiently.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Backend**: Transactions are initiated via the Amazon API Gateway, which routes requests to AWS Lambda functions.  
   - **Data Layer**: Lambda functions write transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker, which normalizes incoming events and writes aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2.  
   - **Security Controls**: All data is encrypted using KMS-managed keys, ensuring confidentiality and integrity.  

3. Journey Name: Financial Report Generation  
   Functionality: Generating and delivering monthly financial reports to users.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Frontend**: Users request a "monthly report" via the web app.  
   - **Backend**: The request is processed by the Amazon API Gateway, which invokes AWS Lambda functions.  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: AWS Step Functions manage the multi-step workflow to aggregate data from Amazon Aurora.  
   - **Data Layer**: The aggregated report data is stored in a private Amazon S3 bucket, ensuring secure access.  
   - **Security Controls**: S3 bucket encryption (AES-256) and IAM controls ensure that only authorized users can access the reports.  

4. Journey Name: Event Notification and Processing  
   Functionality: Handling event notifications and processing them for data insights.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Data Ingestion/Processing**: Amazon SQS receives event notifications from the backend.  
   - **Backend**: AWS Lambda (Worker) normalizes these events and writes the processed data to DynamoDB and Aurora.  
   - **Observability**: Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses, while AWS X-Ray provides request tracing for debugging and performance optimization.  

5. Journey Name: Security and Compliance Management  
   Functionality: Ensuring the security and compliance of the application and its data.  
   Use Case:  
   - **Security Controls**: Encryption is enforced across all data storage solutions, including S3, DynamoDB, and Aurora, using KMS-managed keys. TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission.  
   - **IAM Controls**: Roles are configured with the principle of least privilege, avoiding wildcard actions and ensuring no public S3 buckets.  
   - **Data Classification**: Data is classified based on sensitivity, with PCI-related transaction metadata marked as confidential, user profile information as PII for internal use, and financial reports as highly confidential.  
   - **Networking**: VPC endpoints for DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager ensure secure and private communication within the AWS environment.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing secure access to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services to ensure scalability, security, and global accessibility.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is managed by Amazon Cognito, where users are verified using multi-factor authentication (MFA) for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the application retrieves an IdToken and AccessToken, which are used to securely call the backend API through Amazon API Gateway. The API Gateway, protected by AWS WAF, routes the request to AWS Lambda functions that interact with Amazon DynamoDB to fetch and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and forwards it to a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB, ensuring data integrity and confidentiality through KMS-managed encryption. DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker function that normalizes the transaction data and writes aggregated information to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. This process ensures that transaction data is efficiently processed and stored for further analysis and reporting.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request financial reports, such as a monthly report, through the application interface. The request is handled by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function to initiate a multi-step workflow managed by AWS Step Functions. Step Functions orchestrate the aggregation of data from Amazon Aurora, ensuring that the report generation process is efficient and reliable. The final report is securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, encrypted with AES-256, and accessible only to authorized users, maintaining the confidentiality of highly sensitive financial data.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which acts as a decoupling mechanism to ensure reliable message delivery. AWS Lambda worker functions process these events, normalizing and writing the data to both DynamoDB and Aurora. This ensures that the data pipeline is robust and capable of handling high volumes of transactions without data loss or integrity issues.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of system performance and identification of potential bottlenecks or security issues. This comprehensive monitoring setup ensures that the system remains reliable and secure, with quick detection and response to any anomalies.

6. **Security Controls and Data Protection**: The system employs stringent security controls, including encryption of data at rest and in transit, IAM roles with least privilege access, and no wildcard actions. Public S3 buckets are avoided to prevent unauthorized data access. These measures, combined with VPC endpoints for secure communication with DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager, ensure that sensitive data is protected against unauthorized access and potential breaches.

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend microservice utilizes a React-based web application, which is a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static assets of the application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3. The application is globally delivered using Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and content delivery network (CDN) capabilities to enhance performance and availability.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily processes user interaction data and requests to the backend services. It does not store any sensitive data locally but relies on backend services for data storage and retrieval. The data processed includes user authentication tokens and API requests to access transaction and financial data.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React application.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally with caching capabilities.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the application, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice integrates with Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens. These tokens are used by the application to securely interact with backend services via API Gateway.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and attacks by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Encryption**: Ensures data in transit is protected using TLS 1.2.
   - **IAM Controls**: Implements least privilege access for any AWS resources the frontend may interact with indirectly through backend services.
   - **No public S3 buckets**: Ensures that the S3 bucket hosting the static assets is not publicly accessible, reducing the risk of unauthorized access.

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is handled by Amazon Cognito, where the user is verified through multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP. Upon successful authentication, the application retrieves an IdToken and AccessToken, enabling secure API calls. The API Gateway, protected by AWS WAF, routes requests to AWS Lambda functions, which interact with Amazon DynamoDB to fetch and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and forwards it to a Lambda function. This function writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB, ensuring data is encrypted using KMS-managed keys. DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker that processes the transaction data, normalizing it and writing aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. This ensures that financial data is securely stored and available for reporting.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request monthly financial reports through the application. The request is processed by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function to initiate an AWS Step Functions workflow. This workflow aggregates data from Amazon Aurora, ensuring that the data is encrypted and securely managed. The final report is stored in a private Amazon S3 bucket, encrypted with AES-256, and accessible only to authorized users.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which triggers a Lambda worker to normalize incoming events. The worker writes the processed data to both DynamoDB and Aurora, ensuring that the data pipeline is secure and efficient. AWS Step Functions manage multi-step workflows for complex data processing tasks, ensuring data integrity and availability.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing, allowing for detailed analysis of system performance and potential bottlenecks. This ensures that any issues are quickly identified and resolved, maintaining system reliability and security.

6. **Networking and Security Controls**: The application is deployed within a VPC, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambdas, and public subnets for the NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are used for secure access to DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager. Security controls include encryption for all data at rest and in transit, IAM roles with least privilege, and no public S3 buckets, ensuring that the system is secure against unauthorized access and data breaches.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS, designed to allow authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. User Authentication & Dashboard Access: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication process is managed by Amazon Cognito, where users are authenticated using multi-factor authentication (MFA) for enhanced security. Upon successful authentication, the application obtains an IdToken and AccessToken, allowing the user to securely access the dashboard. The application then calls the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda functions. These functions interact with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. Transaction Processing: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and forwards it to a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which normalizes the incoming event data. The worker function writes the aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further financial reporting and analysis.

3. Financial Report Generation: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. The request is sent to the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. This function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow to manage the multi-step process of aggregating data from Amazon Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is stored in a private Amazon S3 bucket, ensuring that sensitive financial data remains secure and confidential.

4. Data Ingestion & Processing: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS, which queues the events for processing. AWS Lambda worker functions then normalize these events and write the processed data to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora. This ensures that the data is consistently updated and available for real-time analytics and reporting.

5. Observability & Monitoring: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing to help identify and troubleshoot performance bottlenecks and errors within the application, ensuring a reliable and efficient user experience.

6. Security & Compliance: The application employs multiple security controls, including AWS WAF to protect CloudFront with OWASP rules and IP reputation filters. All data is encrypted using KMS-managed keys, and IAM roles are configured with the principle of least privilege to minimize security risks. AWS Secrets Manager manages database passwords and API secrets, ensuring that sensitive information is securely stored and accessed.

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing seamless access to transaction views, payment reconciliation, and financial report generation, all securely hosted on AWS to ensure data integrity and global accessibility.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served globally via Amazon CloudFront. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is generated and securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring that sensitive financial data is protected and accessible only to authorized users.
