# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It provides a user interface for interacting with the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static site, which includes HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, is hosted on Amazon S3. Amazon CloudFront is used to deliver the web application globally with caching capabilities to enhance performance and reduce latency.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice itself does not process or store data directly. Instead, it serves static content and interacts with backend services to fetch and display data to the user. The data displayed includes transaction metadata, user profile information, and financial reports, which are processed and stored by backend services.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static files for the React application.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Distributes the web application globally and caches content for improved performance.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to requests coming through CloudFront.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the application, ensuring users can access the web app via a domain name.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used to authorize API requests. Multi-factor authentication (MFA) is enabled, offering additional security through SMS or TOTP.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and automated attacks by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that the least privilege principle is followed, with no wildcard actions and no public S3 buckets.

## Server Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**:  
   The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to interact with the web application to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**:  
   The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. It is served as static files (HTML, JS, CSS) hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**:  
   The frontend itself does not process or store data persistently. It interacts with backend services to fetch and display data to the user. Any data handling is transient and occurs in the user's browser session.

4. **Integration points with other services**:  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Used to deliver the web application globally with caching, ensuring fast and reliable access for users.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the frontend, ensuring users can access the application via a user-friendly domain name.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the frontend by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web application attacks.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**:  
   The frontend integrates with Amazon Cognito for user authentication. It supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP to enhance security. Upon successful authentication, the frontend obtains ID and Access tokens for API access.

6. **Security controls implemented**:  
   - **AWS WAF**: Provides protection against common web exploits and bots by using OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **CloudFront**: Ensures secure and efficient content delivery with caching and TLS encryption.
   - **S3 Bucket Encryption**: Ensures that the static files are stored securely using AES-256 encryption.

## File System Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for users to interact with the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend microservice utilizes a React-based web application, which is a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. The static assets of the application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3. The application is delivered globally using Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and content delivery network (CDN) capabilities to enhance performance and reduce latency.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily processes user interface data, such as transaction details, financial reports, and user profile information. It does not store any sensitive data locally; instead, it relies on backend services to fetch and display data as needed. The data displayed is classified as PCI-related transaction metadata (confidential), user profile information (PII for internal use), and financial reports (highly confidential).

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   The Frontend microservice integrates with several AWS services to provide its functionality:
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Delivers the web application globally with caching.
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React application.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS for the application.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects CloudFront with OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **Amazon Cognito**: Manages user authentication and authorization.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice uses Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Cognito User Pools are configured with multi-factor authentication (MFA) enabled, using either SMS or TOTP. The application obtains ID and Access tokens from Cognito, which are used to authenticate API requests to the backend services.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   Several security controls are implemented to protect the Frontend microservice:
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and automated bot attacks by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensure least privilege access and prevent wildcard actions.
   - **No public S3 buckets**: Ensures that static assets are not publicly accessible without proper authorization.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing secure access to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services for enhanced performance and security.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user authentication process is initiated when a user opens the client application, which is served via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, where the user is verified using multi-factor authentication (MFA) enabled through SMS or TOTP. Upon successful authentication, the application obtains an IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are then used to call the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda functions. The Lambda functions interact with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display user-specific transaction data on the dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the request is sent through the Amazon API Gateway, which validates the request using Cognito JWT validation. The request is then processed by AWS Lambda functions, which write the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams trigger a Lambda worker that processes the transaction data and writes aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for financial reporting purposes.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. This request is processed by the Amazon API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. The Lambda function triggers AWS Step Functions to manage the multi-step workflow required to aggregate data from Amazon Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring secure access and storage.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. AWS Lambda functions act as workers to normalize these incoming events. The normalized data is then written to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora, ensuring that transaction metadata and financial reporting data are up-to-date and accurate.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is managed through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx errors. AWS X-Ray is used for request tracing, providing insights into the performance and health of the application.

6. **Security and Compliance**: The application enforces security controls such as encryption of S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora using KMS-managed keys. TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission. IAM roles are configured with least privilege access, and no wildcard actions are allowed. Public S3 buckets are prohibited to prevent unauthorized data access.

7. **Networking and Infrastructure**: The application is deployed within a VPC, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambda functions, and public subnets for the NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are configured for DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager to ensure secure and efficient access to AWS services.

   - **S3 Bucket Encryption**: Static assets stored in S3 are encrypted using AES-256 to protect data at rest.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing secure access to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services for enhanced performance and security.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Authentication and Dashboard Access**: The user authentication process is initiated when a user opens the client application, which is served via Amazon CloudFront. The authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, where users are verified using multi-factor authentication (MFA) enabled through SMS or TOTP. Upon successful authentication, the application obtains an IdToken and AccessToken, allowing the user to access the dashboard. The app then calls the API Gateway, which triggers a Lambda function to interact with DynamoDB, retrieving user-specific transaction metadata.

2. **Transaction Processing**: This flow begins when a transaction is initiated through the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. The Lambda function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which normalizes the incoming transaction events and writes aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for financial reporting purposes.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a "monthly report" through the application. This request is processed by the API Gateway, which triggers a Lambda function. The Lambda function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow to manage the multi-step process of aggregating data from Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the result is stored in a private S3 bucket, ensuring that the financial reports are kept highly confidential.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. A Lambda worker function processes these events, normalizing them and writing the relevant data to both DynamoDB and Aurora. This ensures that the data pipeline remains efficient and secure, supporting the backend's event-driven architecture.

5. **Observability and Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray is used for request tracing, providing insights into the application's performance and helping to identify potential bottlenecks or issues in the data flow.

6. **Security and Compliance**: The system employs various security controls, including encryption of S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora using KMS-managed keys. IAM roles are configured with the principle of least privilege, and no wildcard actions are allowed. Public S3 buckets are prohibited to prevent unauthorized access. These measures ensure compliance with data protection standards and mitigate risks associated with unauthorized access or data leakage.

These tokens are then used to call the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda functions. The Lambda functions interact with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the request is sent through the Amazon API Gateway to an AWS Lambda function. The Lambda function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which normalizes the incoming event data. The worker function writes the aggregated data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further financial reporting and analysis.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a "monthly report" through the application. This request is processed by the Amazon API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. The Lambda function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow to manage the multi-step reporting process. Step Functions aggregate the necessary data from Amazon Aurora and store the final report in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring the data is encrypted and securely stored.

4. **Data Ingestion & Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. AWS Lambda worker functions process these events by normalizing the data and writing it to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora. This ensures that transaction metadata and financial reporting data are consistently updated and available for analysis.

5. **Observability & Monitoring**: The system's observability is enhanced through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch Alarms, which monitor Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray is used for request tracing, providing insights into the system's performance and helping to identify potential bottlenecks or issues.

6. **Security Controls & Data Protection**: The system employs various security controls, including encryption of S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora using KMS-managed keys. IAM roles are configured with the principle of least privilege, and no wildcard actions are allowed. Public S3 buckets are prohibited to prevent unauthorized data access. TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission.

7. **Networking & Infrastructure**: The application is deployed within a VPC, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambda functions, and public subnets for the NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are used for DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager to ensure secure and efficient access to these services.

# Microservice Summaries


## Frontend Microservice

1. **Primary functionality and purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It is designed to deliver a seamless user experience by providing a responsive and interactive interface for the FinTech Payments Dashboard.

2. **Technical stack and frameworks used**  
   The Frontend microservice utilizes React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces, particularly single-page applications. The static assets of the React application, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files, are hosted on Amazon S3.

3. **Data processed and stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily handles static content and does not process or store dynamic data directly. However, it interacts with backend services to fetch and display user-specific data such as transaction details and financial reports.

4. **Integration points with other services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: The web application is delivered globally through Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and improves load times for users worldwide.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Handles DNS routing for the application, ensuring users are directed to the correct resources.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the application by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web exploits and attacks.

5. **Authentication mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used to authorize API requests. Multi-factor authentication (MFA) is enabled to enhance security.

6. **Security controls implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web vulnerabilities and attacks.
   - **Encryption**: S3 buckets are encrypted using AES-256 to secure static assets.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures least privilege access to AWS resources, preventing unauthorized access to the infrastructure.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.

## Server Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The Frontend microservice is responsible for delivering the user interface of the FinTech Payments Dashboard. It allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports through a React-based web application.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The frontend is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces. It is served as static content, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The frontend does not process or store data directly. It serves static files and interacts with backend services to display dynamic content to users.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - The frontend is hosted on Amazon S3 and delivered globally via Amazon CloudFront, which provides caching and content delivery.
   - It integrates with Amazon Route 53 for DNS management.
   - The frontend communicates with the backend services through API Gateway for dynamic data retrieval and user interactions.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - User authentication is managed through Amazon Cognito User Pool, which supports multi-factor authentication (MFA) using SMS or TOTP.
   - The frontend obtains ID and Access tokens from Cognito for authenticated API calls.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - AWS WAF is used to protect CloudFront with OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate automated bot attacks and other threats.
   - TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission.
   - The S3 bucket hosting the static site is encrypted using AES-256.

## File System Microservice

1. **Primary Functionality and Purpose**  
   The primary functionality of the Frontend microservice is to serve a React-based web application that allows authenticated users to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports. It provides a user interface for interacting with the serverless backend services.

2. **Technical Stack and Frameworks Used**  
   - **React**: The web application is built using React, a popular JavaScript library for building user interfaces.
   - **Amazon S3**: Hosts the static assets of the React site, including HTML, JavaScript, and CSS files.
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: A content delivery network (CDN) that delivers the web application globally with caching to improve performance and reduce latency.

3. **Data Processed and Stored**  
   The Frontend microservice primarily handles static assets and does not process or store user data directly. It serves the static files necessary for rendering the web application in users' browsers.

4. **Integration Points with Other Services**  
   - **Amazon CloudFront**: Integrates with CloudFront to deliver the web application globally.
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to mitigate common web application attacks.
   - **Amazon Route 53**: Manages DNS for the web application, ensuring users can access the application via a domain name.

5. **Authentication Mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice itself does not handle authentication directly but relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides tokens that the frontend uses to interact with backend services securely.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects the CloudFront distribution with web application firewall rules to prevent attacks such as SQL injection and cross-site scripting (XSS).
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure communication between users' browsers and the CloudFront distribution.
   - **Amazon S3 Bucket Policies**: Ensure that the S3 bucket hosting the static assets is not publicly accessible, preventing unauthorized access to the application files.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services to ensure scalability, security, and global accessibility.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates the login process by accessing the client application through Amazon CloudFront. Authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, which verifies the user's credentials and provides an IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are used by the application to securely call the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda. The Lambda function retrieves user-specific data from Amazon DynamoDB, allowing the user to access their personalized dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the request is sent to the Amazon API Gateway, which triggers an AWS Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which processes the stream data and writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further analysis and reporting.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. This request is sent to the Amazon API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function. The Lambda function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow that aggregates the necessary data from Amazon Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is stored in a private Amazon S3 bucket, ensuring secure access and storage.

4. **Data Ingestion & Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. An AWS Lambda worker function processes these events, normalizing the data and writing it to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora. This ensures that all incoming data is correctly formatted and stored for future use.

5. **Observability & Monitoring**: The system's observability is managed through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray is used for request tracing, providing detailed insights into the application's performance and helping to identify any potential issues.

6. **Security & Compliance**: The application employs multiple security controls, including AWS WAF for protecting CloudFront, encryption for S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora using KMS-managed keys, and enforcing TLS 1.2 for secure data transmission. IAM roles are configured with least privilege access, and no wildcard actions or public S3 buckets are allowed, ensuring compliance with security best practices.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application deployed on AWS that enables authenticated users to securely view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, enhancing financial management and operational efficiency for businesses.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates the login process by accessing the client application through Amazon CloudFront. Authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, which verifies the user's credentials and provides an IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are used by the application to securely call the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to an AWS Lambda function. The Lambda function interacts with Amazon DynamoDB to retrieve and display the user's transaction data on the dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the request is sent to the Amazon API Gateway, which forwards it to an AWS Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams trigger another Lambda worker function that processes the stream data and writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further analysis and reporting.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. The request is sent to the Amazon API Gateway, which triggers a Lambda function. This function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow that aggregates the necessary data from Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring secure access and storage.

4. **Data Ingestion & Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. An AWS Lambda worker function normalizes these incoming events and writes the processed data to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora Serverless v2. This ensures that all transaction and reporting data is up-to-date and available for analysis.

5. **Observability & Monitoring**: The system's observability is managed through Amazon CloudWatch Logs and CloudWatch Alarms, which monitor for Lambda errors and API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray is used for request tracing, providing insights into the performance and health of the application.

6. **Security Controls**: The application employs multiple security measures, including encryption of S3 buckets, DynamoDB, and Aurora data using KMS-managed keys. TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission. IAM roles are configured with least privilege access, and no wildcard actions are allowed. Public S3 buckets are avoided to prevent unauthorized data access.

7. **Networking & Infrastructure**: The application is deployed within a VPC, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambda functions, and public subnets for the NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are used for secure access to DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager, ensuring that data remains within the AWS network.

8. **Authentication & Authorization**: Amazon Cognito User Pool is used for user authentication, with MFA enabled for added security. The system ensures secure token-based authentication flows, providing temporary AWS IAM credentials through Cognito Identity Pool for accessing AWS resources.

5. **Authentication Mechanisms**  
   The Frontend microservice relies on Amazon Cognito for user authentication and authorization. Users authenticate through Cognito, which provides ID and Access tokens used by the frontend to interact with backend services securely.

6. **Security Controls Implemented**  
   - **AWS WAF**: Protects against common web exploits and bots by applying OWASP rules and IP reputation filters.
   - **TLS 1.2**: Enforced for secure data transmission between the client and the server.
   - **IAM Controls**: Ensures that only authorized services and users can access the resources necessary for the frontend to function.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing a secure platform to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, leveraging AWS's managed services for enhanced performance and security.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates access to the FinTech Payments Dashboard by opening the client application, which is served through Amazon CloudFront. Authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, where the user is verified and provided with IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are used by the application to securely call the backend API via Amazon API Gateway, which then triggers AWS Lambda functions to interact with Amazon DynamoDB, retrieving and displaying transaction metadata on the user's dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the API Gateway receives the request and invokes a Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the relevant metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which processes the stream data and writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further financial reporting and analysis.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. This request is processed by the API Gateway, which invokes a Lambda function to start an AWS Step Functions workflow. The workflow aggregates necessary data from Amazon Aurora and processes it to generate the report. The final report is securely stored in an Amazon S3 private bucket, ensuring that only authorized users can access it.

4. **Data Ingestion and Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are sent to Amazon SQS, which queues the events for processing. An AWS Lambda worker function retrieves these events, normalizes the data, and writes it to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora, ensuring that all transaction and reporting data is up-to-date and consistent across the system.

5. **Security and Observability**: The system is protected by AWS WAF, which applies OWASP rules and IP reputation filters to safeguard against common web threats. Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms monitor the system for errors and anomalies, while AWS X-Ray provides request tracing to help diagnose and resolve issues quickly. IAM roles are configured with the principle of least privilege to minimize the risk of unauthorized access.

6. **Networking and Data Security**: The application operates within a VPC, with private subnets for Aurora and Lambda functions, and public subnets for the NAT gateway. VPC Endpoints are used for secure access to DynamoDB, S3, and Secrets Manager. All data is encrypted using KMS-managed keys, and TLS 1.2 is enforced for secure data transmission. IAM policies are carefully managed to avoid misconfigurations and ensure that no S3 buckets are publicly accessible.

# Introduction

The FinTech Payments Dashboard is a serverless web application designed to empower authenticated users by providing seamless access to view transactions, reconcile payments, and generate financial reports, all while ensuring robust security and global accessibility through AWS managed services.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Login & Dashboard Access**: The user initiates the login process by accessing the client application through Amazon CloudFront. Authentication is handled by Amazon Cognito, which verifies the user's credentials and provides an IdToken and AccessToken. These tokens are used by the application to securely call the Amazon API Gateway, which routes the request to AWS Lambda. The Lambda function retrieves user-specific data from Amazon DynamoDB, allowing the user to access their personalized dashboard.

2. **Transaction Processing**: When a transaction is initiated, the request is sent to Amazon API Gateway, which triggers an AWS Lambda function. This function processes the transaction and writes the transaction metadata to Amazon DynamoDB. DynamoDB Streams then trigger a Lambda worker function, which processes the stream data and writes aggregated transaction data to Amazon Aurora Serverless v2 for further analysis and reporting.

3. **Financial Report Generation**: Users can request a monthly financial report through the application. The request is sent to Amazon API Gateway, which invokes an AWS Lambda function. This function initiates an AWS Step Functions workflow that aggregates the necessary data from Amazon Aurora. Once the data is aggregated, the final report is stored in a private Amazon S3 bucket, ensuring secure access and storage.

4. **Data Ingestion & Processing**: Event notifications from the backend are received by Amazon SQS. An AWS Lambda worker function processes these events, normalizing the data and writing it to both Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora. This ensures that all data is consistently processed and stored for future use.

5. **Observability & Monitoring**: Amazon CloudWatch Logs and Alarms are used to monitor the system for errors and performance issues, such as Lambda function errors or API Gateway 5xx responses. AWS X-Ray provides request tracing to help identify and troubleshoot issues within the application, ensuring smooth operation and quick resolution of any problems.

6. **Security & Compliance**: The system employs multiple security controls, including AWS WAF for protecting CloudFront, encryption for data at rest and in transit, and IAM roles with least privilege access. AWS Secrets Manager manages sensitive information like database passwords and API secrets, ensuring they are securely stored and accessed only by authorized components.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, while empowering bank staff with administrative controls and reporting tools to enhance operational efficiency and customer service.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers initiate the registration process via the web or mobile UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service, which handles user authentication and token generation. Successful registration allows users to log in and access their accounts securely.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Once logged in, customers can create new accounts or view existing account details. The Account Service manages account creation and retrieves account information from the database, ensuring users have a comprehensive overview of their financial status.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers through the UI. The request is processed by the API Gateway and validated by the Auth Service. The Transaction Service checks account balances and recipient details before executing the transfer. The Notification Service sends confirmation messages, and the Audit Service logs the transaction for compliance.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history via the UI. The Transaction Service retrieves transaction records from the database, and the data is formatted for display or download, ensuring users have access to their financial activities.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): The Notification Service sends alerts and confirmations to users via SMS, email, or push notifications. Integration with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service ensures timely and reliable delivery of messages.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and resolution. Support staff can view and manage tickets, ensuring efficient handling of customer queries and issues.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access the dashboard to manage user accounts and monitor transactions. The Admin Service provides tools for user management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight, ensuring secure and compliant operations.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on user activity and transactions using the Reporting Service. The Audit Service logs all actions for compliance, providing a comprehensive view of system activities for regulatory adherence.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

It also interacts with external systems like the RBI Payment Gateway for interbank transfers and the SMS/Email services for notifications.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The Frontend microservice utilizes token-based authentication, likely using OAuth 2.0, to ensure secure access to the application. Users must authenticate via the Auth Service, which validates tokens for each session. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) may also be implemented to enhance security.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - The Frontend microservice implements several security controls, including HTTPS for secure communication, input validation to prevent injection attacks, and adherence to WCAG 2.1 compliance for accessibility. Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) is used to manage user permissions, and all user accounts are stored using SHA1 hash for password security. # Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, while providing bank staff with administrative controls and reporting tools to enhance operational efficiency and customer support.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers initiate the registration process via the web or mobile UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service, which handles user authentication and token generation. Successful registration allows users to log in and access their accounts securely.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Once logged in, customers can create new accounts or view existing ones. The Account Service manages account data, ensuring users have a comprehensive overview of their financial status.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers through the UI. The request is processed by the API Gateway, authenticated by the Auth Service, and validated by the Transaction Service. For inter-bank transfers, the RBI Payment Gateway is used. The Notification Service confirms the transaction to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history via the UI. The Transaction Service retrieves data from the database, ensuring users have access to their financial activities.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): The Notification Service sends transaction confirmations and alerts via SMS, email, or push notifications. Integration with the SMS Gateway and Email Service ensures timely delivery.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages these requests, allowing support staff to view and resolve issues efficiently.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access the dashboard to manage user accounts and transactions. The Admin Service provides tools for user management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity using the Reporting Service. The Audit Service ensures all actions are logged for compliance and review purposes.

The Transaction Service checks account balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The Notification Service sends confirmation to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): The Notification Service sends alerts and confirmations to users via SMS, email, or push notifications. Integration with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service ensures timely delivery of messages.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and resolution. Support staff can view and manage tickets to assist customers effectively.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access the dashboard to manage user accounts and monitor transactions. The Admin Service provides tools for user management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity using the Reporting Service. The Audit Service logs all significant actions for compliance and review purposes.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with an intuitive online banking experience while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated by the Auth Service. Successful registration or login results in user data being stored in the database, and a session token is generated for subsequent interactions.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view their account details. The UI collects necessary information, which is processed by the Account Service. The service ensures compliance with KYC requirements via integration with the KYC Provider. Account details are stored in the database and can be retrieved for display on the user's dashboard.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers through the UI. The request is routed via the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks the user's balance and validates the recipient's details. For inter-bank transfers, the RBI Payment Gateway is used. Upon successful execution, the transaction is logged in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data, which is retrieved from the database by the Transaction Service. The data is formatted and presented to the user, with options for downloading in various formats.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Notifications are sent to users for various events, such as successful fund transfers. The Notification Service integrates with the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages. The service ensures messages are sent promptly and logs notification events for auditing purposes.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets via the UI. The Ticketing Service processes these requests, storing ticket details in the database. Support staff can view and manage tickets through the Admin Dashboard, ensuring timely resolution of customer issues.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The Admin Service provides functionalities for creating, editing, or disabling user accounts and viewing transaction details. Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) ensures that only authorized personnel can perform specific actions.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators can generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service aggregates data from various sources, allowing for custom report generation. The Audit Service logs all significant actions for compliance and review purposes.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, while providing bank staff with administrative controls and reporting tools to enhance customer support and operational efficiency.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers initiate the registration process via the web or mobile UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service, which handles user authentication and token generation. Successful registration allows users to log in and access their accounts securely.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Once logged in, customers can create new accounts or view existing ones. The Account Service manages account details and provides an overview of account balances and recent transactions.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers through the UI. The request is processed by the API Gateway and validated by the Auth Service. The Transaction Service checks account balances and recipient details before executing the transfer. The Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history via the UI. The Transaction Service retrieves transaction records from the database, and the data is presented to the user in a downloadable format.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): The Notification Service sends alerts and confirmations to users via SMS, email, or push notifications. Integration with external services like SMS Gateway and Email Service ensures timely delivery.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and resolution. Support staff can view and manage tickets to assist customers effectively.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access the dashboard to manage user accounts and transactions. The Admin Service provides tools for user management, role-based access control, and transaction monitoring.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity using the Reporting Service. The Audit Service logs all activities for compliance and security purposes, ensuring adherence to regulatory requirements.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with intuitive online banking solutions while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated by the Auth Service. Successful registration or login results in a session token being issued.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers create and view their account details. The UI collects necessary information, which is processed by the Account Service. The service ensures data integrity and stores account details in the database.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway, where the Auth Service validates the token. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is logged in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data, which the Transaction Service retrieves from the database. The data is formatted and sent back to the UI for display or download.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Notifications are sent to customers for various activities. The Notification Service receives triggers from other services (e.g., Transaction Service) and sends messages via the SMS Gateway or Email Service.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service processes these requests, storing them in the database. Support staff can view and manage tickets via the Admin Dashboard.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Admins access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The UI interacts with the User Management and Transaction Services to perform actions like creating, editing, or disabling accounts and viewing transaction details.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Admins generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service aggregates data from various sources, formats it, and provides it to the UI. The Audit Service logs all actions for compliance and review purposes.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, while providing bank staff with administrative controls and reporting tools to enhance operational efficiency and customer support.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated by the Auth Service. Successful registration and login are confirmed via the Notification Service.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Users can create and view their account details. The UI collects necessary information, which is processed by the Account Service. The data is stored in the database, and users receive confirmation through the Notification Service.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway, where the Auth Service validates the token. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is logged by the Audit Service, and a confirmation is sent via the Notification Service.

4. Transaction History and Download: Users can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data, which is retrieved from the database by the Transaction Service. The data is formatted and sent to the user, with a download option available.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Notifications are sent to users for various activities. The Notification Service integrates with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Users can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages these tickets, allowing support staff to view and respond to them. All interactions are logged for audit purposes.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Admins access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The Admin Service provides functionalities for creating, editing, or disabling user accounts and monitoring transactions. All actions are logged by the Audit Service.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Admins generate reports on transactions and user activities. The Reporting Service compiles data from various sources, allowing admins to create custom reports. The Audit Service ensures all activities are logged for compliance and review.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with seamless online banking experiences while providing bank staff with essential administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Users can register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then sent to the Auth Service for validation and token generation. Successful registration or login results in a session token being issued to the user.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Users can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI sends requests to the Account Service, which manages account data and retrieves account information from the database for display.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Users initiate fund transfers through the UI. The request is routed via the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks the user's balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. 5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Users receive notifications for various activities. The Notification Service interfaces with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to send messages based on triggers from other services, such as successful fund transfers or account updates.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Users can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and retrieval, allowing support staff to view and respond to user queries.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The Admin Service provides functionalities for user account management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight, interfacing with the User and Transaction Services.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on user activity and transactions. The Reporting Service aggregates data from various services and formats it into customizable reports. The Audit Service logs all significant actions for compliance and review purposes.

It involves redirecting users to an authentication page, obtaining an access token upon successful login, and using this token for subsequent API requests. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) is also implemented to enhance security.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - The Frontend microservice implements several security controls, including:
     - HTTPS for secure data transmission.
     - Content Security Policy (CSP) to prevent cross-site scripting (XSS) attacks.
     - Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) policies to control resource access.
     - Input validation and sanitization to prevent injection attacks.
     - Secure handling of tokens and sensitive data in browser storage.
     - Regular security audits and vulnerability assessments as part of the CI/CD pipeline.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with an intuitive online banking experience while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts securely. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated and stored by the User Management Service. Authentication tokens are generated by the Auth Service for secure session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view their account details. The Account Service handles account creation requests, while the Overview Service retrieves and displays account information to the user.

3. Fund Transfer (Intra-bank and Inter-bank): Customers can transfer funds to other accounts. The UI captures transfer details, which are routed through the API Gateway. The Auth Service validates the user's token, and the Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The Transaction History Service retrieves transaction data from the database and formats it for display or download.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Customers receive notifications for various activities. The Notification Service integrates with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to send notifications via the appropriate channels.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets for assistance. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and resolution, allowing support staff to view and manage tickets.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators can manage users and transactions through a dedicated dashboard. The Admin Dashboard Service provides interfaces for user management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators can generate reports and audit logs. The Reporting Service allows for the creation of custom reports on transactions and user activity, while the Audit Service maintains logs for compliance and monitoring purposes.

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User contact information and notification content

   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

# Introduction

The Serverless Reference Architecture: Web Application is a general-purpose, event-driven web application back-end that leverages AWS Lambda, Amazon API Gateway, Amazon DynamoDB, and Amazon Cognito to provide a secure and scalable solution for managing user-specific To Do items, enabling registered users to seamlessly create, update, view, and delete their tasks while ensuring data privacy and efficient user management.

# Functional Flows

1. **User Registration and Authentication:**
   - **Functionality:** Users register and authenticate to access the ToDo application.
   - **Use Case:** The application uses Amazon Cognito User Pools to manage user registration and authentication. Users register by providing their details, and upon successful registration, they can log in. Once authenticated, users receive a JWT token, which is used for subsequent API calls to ensure secure access to their personal ToDo items.

2. **Front End Application:**
   - **Functionality:** Provides the user interface for interacting with the ToDo application.
   - **Use Case:** The front-end application, built with create-react-app, serves static content such as HTML, CSS, JavaScript, and images. These resources are hosted on AWS Amplify Console and are downloaded to the user's browser when they access the application. The front-end communicates with the backend via REST API calls to perform operations like listing, adding, updating, and deleting ToDo items.

3. **Back End Application (Business Logic):**
   - **Functionality:** Implements the core business logic of the ToDo application.
   - **Use Case:** The backend is composed of AWS Lambda functions, each responsible for a specific operation: listing all ToDo items, retrieving details of a specific item, updating an item, creating a new item, marking an item as complete, and deleting an item. These functions are accessed through an API Gateway REST API. The application stores all ToDo items in a DynamoDB table, ensuring efficient data management and retrieval.

4. **Data Storage:**
   - **Functionality:** Stores and manages ToDo items for all users.
   - **Use Case:** Amazon DynamoDB is used as the database to store ToDo items. Each user's items are stored securely, and access is restricted to authenticated users only. The database supports operations such as adding, updating, retrieving, and deleting items, ensuring data integrity and availability.

5. **Deployment and Management:**
   - **Functionality:** Manages the deployment and updates of the application.
   - **Use Case:** AWS Amplify Console is used to manage the deployment of the front-end application. It automatically deploys updates when changes are pushed to the connected GitHub repository. The backend is deployed using AWS SAM, which packages and deploys the Lambda functions and associated resources. This setup ensures a streamlined and automated deployment process, reducing manual intervention and potential errors.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: GitHub
   - Purpose of integration: Source code repository and version control for the application.
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: Personal Access Token
   - Data shared with the third party: Source code and configuration files.

2. Name of the third-party service: AWS Amplify Console
   - Purpose of integration: Hosting and deployment of the front-end application.
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: IAM Role (AmplifyRole)
   - Data shared with the third party: Front-end application files and deployment configurations.

3. Name of the third-party service: AWS Lambda
   - Purpose of integration: Execution of backend business logic.
   - Type of integration: SDK
   - Authentication method used: IAM Role
   - Data shared with the third party: Backend application code and execution context.

4. Name of the third-party service: Amazon API Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Exposing REST API endpoints for the application.
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: IAM Role
   - Data shared with the third party: API requests and responses.

5. Name of the third-party service: Amazon DynamoDB
   - Purpose of integration: Storage of ToDo items.
   - Type of integration: SDK
   - Authentication method used: IAM Role
   - Data shared with the third party: ToDo item data.

6. Name of the third-party service: Amazon Cognito
   - Purpose of integration: User registration and authentication.
   - Type of integration: API
   - Authentication method used: JWT Token
   - Data shared with the third party: User authentication data and tokens.

## Frontend Microservice

It serves as the user interface for the application, allowing users to interact with the To Do app by creating, updating, viewing, and deleting items.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The frontend is built using the `create-react-app` framework, which is a popular tool for setting up a React.js application with a modern build setup. The static content generated by this framework is hosted on AWS Amplify Console.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The Frontend microservice does not directly process or store data. Instead, it interacts with the backend services via REST API calls to perform operations on the To Do items. The actual data processing and storage are handled by the backend services and the DynamoDB database.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - The frontend communicates with the backend application through REST API calls. These calls are made to the API Gateway, which fronts the Lambda functions implementing the business logic.
   - It also integrates with AWS Amplify Console for hosting and deploying the static content.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - User authentication is managed through Amazon Cognito User Pools. Once a user is authenticated, the frontend receives a JWT token, which is then used to authenticate subsequent API requests to the backend services.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - The frontend relies on HTTPS for secure communication between the client and the server.
   - It uses JWT tokens for authenticating API requests, ensuring that only authenticated users can access their own To Do items.
   - The Amplify Console manages the deployment of frontend updates, ensuring that only authorized changes are deployed to the production environment.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with an intuitive online banking experience while providing bank staff with essential administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process begins with the user interface (UI) capturing user details, which are then sent to the API Gateway. The Auth Service validates the credentials and generates a token for session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI sends requests to the API Gateway, which routes them to the Account Service. The service manages account data and retrieves information from the database for display.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway, where the Auth Service validates the token. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transaction. The transaction is stored in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user. The Audit Service logs the transaction for compliance.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway, which is processed by the Transaction Service. The service retrieves the data from the database and formats it for download.

5. Notifications: Customers receive notifications via SMS, email, or push notifications. The Notification Service integrates with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The request is processed by the Ticketing Service, which manages ticket data and assigns it to support staff for resolution.

7. Admin Dashboard: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The UI interacts with the Admin Service via the API Gateway, allowing admins to perform actions like user management and transaction monitoring.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service processes requests from the UI, retrieves data from the database, and formats it for compliance and analysis.

9. Identity Verification: The KYC Provider is integrated for identity verification during user registration. The Auth Service communicates with the KYC Provider using OAuth-API to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

10. Fraud Detection: The Fraud Detection Engine checks for transaction anomalies. The Transaction Service publishes transaction data to a Kafka topic, which the Fraud Detection Engine monitors for suspicious activity.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers a secure and seamless banking experience, enabling customers to manage accounts, transfer funds, and access transaction history through intuitive web and mobile interfaces, while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated and stored by the User Management Service. Authentication tokens are generated by the Auth Service for secure access.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The Account Service handles the creation and retrieval of account information, ensuring data is securely stored and accessible.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway, where the Auth Service validates the token. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer and storing the transaction in the database. The Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The Transaction Service retrieves transaction data, which is then formatted and presented to the user via the UI.

5. Notifications: Customers receive notifications via SMS, email, or push notifications. The Notification Service integrates with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The Ticket Management Service handles the creation, viewing, and management of tickets, allowing support staff to assist with queries.

7. Admin Dashboard: Administrators can manage users and transactions through a dedicated dashboard. The Admin Service provides functionalities for user management, role-based access control, and transaction oversight.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators can generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service aggregates data and generates custom reports, while the Audit Service ensures all actions are logged for compliance.

9. Identity Verification: The KYC Provider is integrated for identity verification during user registration. The Auth Service communicates with the KYC Provider via OAuth-API to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

10. Fraud Detection: Transactions are monitored for anomalies using the Fraud Detection Engine. The Transaction Service publishes transaction data to a Kafka topic, where the Fraud Detection Engine analyzes it for potential fraud.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, to enhance the online banking experience for customers and provide bank staff with essential administrative tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process begins with the user interface (UI) capturing user details, which are then sent through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for validation and token generation. Successful registration or login allows access to the banking platform.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI sends requests through the API Gateway to the Account Service, which manages account data and provides an overview of account balances and recent transactions.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service then checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is recorded in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user. The Audit Service logs the transaction for compliance.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway, which is fetched from the Transaction Service. The data is formatted and sent back to the user for viewing or downloading.

5. Notifications: Customers receive notifications via SMS, email, or push notifications. The Notification Service interfaces with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The request is processed by the Ticketing Service, which allows support staff to view and manage tickets. All reviewers have access to view all tickets for efficient resolution.

7. Admin Dashboard: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The UI interacts with the Admin Service to perform actions like creating, editing, or disabling user accounts, and generating reports on transactions and user activity.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate custom reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service aggregates data and allows for special character searches to identify edge cases. The Audit Service ensures all actions are logged for compliance.

9. Identity Verification: The KYC Provider is used for identity verification during user registration. The Auth Service integrates with the KYC Provider using OAuth-API to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

10. Fraud Detection: The Fraud Detection Engine checks for transaction anomalies. The Transaction Service publishes transaction data to a Kafka topic, which the Fraud Detection Engine monitors for suspicious activity, raising alerts as necessary.

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification
