# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, to provide customers with a seamless online banking experience.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process begins with the user interface (UI) capturing user details, which are then sent to the API Gateway. The Auth Service validates the credentials and issues a token for session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI sends requests to the API Gateway, which routes them to the Account Service. The service manages account data and retrieves information from the database for display.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer and updating the database. The Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway, which the Transaction Service retrieves from the database. The data is formatted and sent back to the UI for display or download.

5. Notifications: Customers receive notifications via SMS, email, or push notifications. The Notification Service interfaces with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The request is processed by the Ticketing Service, which stores the ticket in the database. Support staff can view and manage tickets through the Admin Dashboard.

7. Admin Dashboard: Administrators manage user roles, permissions, and transactions. The Admin Dashboard interfaces with various services like User Management and Reporting to provide comprehensive management tools.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service aggregates data from the database, allowing for custom report generation. The Audit Service logs all significant actions for compliance and review.

9. Interbank Transfer: For interbank transfers, the Transaction Service interfaces with the RBI Payment Gateway using REST APIs to route transactions securely.

10. Identity Verification: The KYC Provider is used for identity verification during user registration. The Auth Service integrates with the KYC Provider using OAuth-API to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

   - The UI Service implements several security controls, including HTTPS for secure data transmission, input validation to prevent injection attacks, and adherence to WCAG 2.1 for accessibility compliance. Additionally, it relies on backend services for robust access control and audit logging to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements such as PCI DSS and GDPR.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and intuitive personal banking functionalities, such as account management and fund transfers, empowering customers with a seamless banking experience while providing bank staff with essential administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process begins with the user interface (UI) where customers input their details. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service, which validates the credentials and generates a token for session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view their account details. The UI collects necessary information, which is processed through the API Gateway. The Account Service manages account creation and retrieves account details from the database for display.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is recorded in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user. The Audit Service logs the transaction for compliance.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway. The Transaction Service retrieves the data from the database, and the UI formats it for display or download.

5. Notifications: Customers receive notifications via SMS, email, or push notifications. The Notification Service integrates with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets through the UI. The request is processed through the API Gateway to the Support Service, which manages ticket creation and updates. Support staff can view and manage tickets via the Admin Dashboard.

7. Admin Dashboard: Administrators manage user roles, permissions, and transactions. The Admin Dashboard interfaces with the User Management and Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) services to perform these tasks. The Reporting Service generates compliance and activity reports for administrators.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators can generate custom reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service processes requests from the Admin Dashboard, retrieves data from the database, and formats it for reporting. The Audit Service logs all relevant activities for compliance purposes.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

## UI SERVICE Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The UI Service is designed to provide a web and mobile interface for NextBank's digital banking platform. It facilitates user interactions for functionalities such as account management, fund transfers, transaction history, and notifications. The service ensures that the user interface is intuitive, responsive, and compliant with accessibility standards.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The UI Service is likely built using modern web technologies such as React or Angular for the web interface and React Native or Flutter for the mobile interface. These frameworks are chosen for their ability to create dynamic, responsive, and cross-platform applications. The service may also utilize CSS frameworks like Bootstrap or Tailwind for styling and ensuring WCAG 2.1 compliance.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The UI Service processes user input data such as login credentials, transaction details, and user preferences. It does not store sensitive data locally but interacts with backend services to fetch and display data securely. Any temporary data storage is handled using secure session management techniques.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - The UI Service integrates with several backend microservices via the API Gateway. Key integrations include:
     - Auth Service for user authentication and token validation.
     - Transaction Service for initiating and managing fund transfers.
     - Notification Service for sending confirmation messages.
     - Reporting and Audit Services for displaying user activity and compliance reports.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The UI Service utilizes OAuth 2.0 for secure authentication, ensuring that user credentials are never exposed. It relies on the Auth Service to validate tokens and manage user sessions. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) may be implemented to enhance security for sensitive operations.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - The UI Service implements several security controls to protect user data and interactions:
     - HTTPS is enforced for all communications to prevent data interception.
     - Input validation and sanitization are performed to prevent injection attacks.
     - Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) and Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF) protections are in place.
     - Regular security audits and vulnerability assessments are conducted to identify and mitigate potential threats.
     - Compliance with GDPR and other relevant data protection regulations is ensured to safeguard user privacy.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform designed to offer customers a secure and seamless banking experience by providing functionalities such as account management, fund transfers, and transaction history, while equipping bank staff with essential administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are sent to the API Gateway. The Auth Service validates credentials and issues a token for session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers create and view their account details. The UI sends requests through the API Gateway to the Account Service, which manages account data and retrieves account summaries from the database.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks balance and recipient details, executes the transfer, and updates the database. The Notification Service sends a confirmation, and the Audit Service logs the transaction.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway, which the Transaction Service retrieves from the database and formats for display or download.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Notifications are sent to users for various events. The Notification Service integrates with the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages, using HTTP-based API and SMTP/API methods, respectively.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers submit support tickets via the UI. The Ticketing Service manages these requests, allowing support staff to view and manage tickets. All reviewers have access to all tickets for comprehensive support.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators use the dashboard to manage users and transactions. The UI interacts with the User Management and Transaction Services via the API Gateway to perform actions like creating, editing, or disabling user accounts and monitoring transactions.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activity. The Reporting Service processes requests from the UI, accessing transaction data and user activity logs to create custom reports, which are then delivered to the admin.

9. Identity Verification: The KYC Provider is used for identity verification during user registration. The Auth Service integrates with the KYC Provider using OAuth-API to ensure compliance with regulatory requirements.

10. Fraud Detection: The Fraud Detection Engine checks for transaction anomalies. The Transaction Service publishes transaction data to a Kafka topic, which the Fraud Detection Engine monitors to identify and alert on suspicious activities.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User contact information and notification content

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

     - HTTPS is used for all communications to encrypt data in transit.
     - Input validation and sanitization are performed to prevent injection attacks.
     - Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) is enforced to restrict access to sensitive features based on user roles.
     - Regular security testing and vulnerability assessments are conducted as part of the CI/CD pipeline to identify and mitigate potential security risks.

## THIRD-PARTY SERVICES Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The UI Service is responsible for providing the web and mobile interfaces for the NextBank digital banking platform. It facilitates user interactions for functionalities such as user registration, login, account management, fund transfers, transaction history viewing, and notifications.

   - Auth Service: Validates user tokens for secure access.
   - API Gateway: Routes requests from the UI to appropriate backend services.
   - Notification Service: Sends confirmation and alert notifications to users.
   - Transaction Service: Facilitates fund transfers and transaction history retrieval.
   - Audit Service: Logs user actions for compliance and monitoring.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The UI Service uses token-based authentication, likely leveraging JWT (JSON Web Tokens) to manage user sessions securely. It integrates with the Auth Service to validate tokens and ensure secure access to user accounts.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - HTTPS is enforced for all communications to protect data in transit.
   - Input validation and sanitization are implemented to prevent injection attacks.
   - CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery) protection is in place to secure user sessions.
   - Content Security Policy (CSP) is configured to mitigate XSS (Cross-Site Scripting) attacks.
   - Regular security audits and vulnerability assessments are conducted to ensure the UI Service remains secure against emerging threats.

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform that offers secure and seamless personal banking functionalities, enabling customers to manage accounts, transfer funds, and access transaction history while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then validated by the Auth Service. Successful registration or login results in user session creation and token generation.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI collects necessary information, which is processed by the Account Service. The service interacts with the Database to store and retrieve account information.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway, where the Auth Service validates the token. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is logged in the Database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user. The Audit Service logs the transaction for compliance.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data, which the Transaction Service retrieves from the Database. The data is formatted and sent back to the UI for display or download.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Customers receive notifications for various activities. The Notification Service interfaces with the SMS Gateway and Email Service to send messages. The service ensures timely delivery of notifications based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers submit support tickets via the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation, updates, and resolution. Support staff can view and manage tickets, ensuring customer issues are addressed promptly.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The Admin Service provides functionalities for user management, role assignment, and transaction monitoring. The service ensures compliance with RBAC policies.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activities. The Reporting Service aggregates data from various sources, allowing admins to create custom reports. The Audit Service logs all activities for compliance and regulatory purposes.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User contact information and notification content

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

## UI SERVICE Microservice

1. Primary functionality and purpose:
   - The UI Service is designed to provide a seamless and intuitive user interface for both web and mobile platforms. It facilitates user interactions with the NextBank application, allowing customers to perform banking operations such as account management, fund transfers, and viewing transaction history. It also provides interfaces for bank staff and administrators to access administrative controls and reporting tools.

2. Technical stack and frameworks used:
   - The UI Service is likely built using modern web technologies such as React or Angular for the web interface and React Native or Flutter for the mobile interface. These frameworks are chosen for their ability to create responsive and dynamic user interfaces. The service is containerized using Docker and managed via Kubernetes (EKS) for scalability and deployment efficiency.

3. Data processed and stored:
   - The UI Service processes user input data such as login credentials, transaction details, and user preferences. It does not store sensitive data directly but interacts with backend services to fetch and display data securely. Any temporary data storage is handled in compliance with security best practices to ensure data protection.

4. Integration points with other services:
   - The UI Service integrates with several backend microservices through the API Gateway. Key integration points include:
     - Auth Service for user authentication and token validation.
     - Transaction Service for executing and retrieving transaction details.
     - Notification Service for sending confirmation messages to users.
     - Audit Service for logging user activities.

5. Authentication mechanisms:
   - The UI Service utilizes token-based authentication, where user credentials are validated by the Auth Service, and a secure token is issued for session management. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) is implemented to enhance security, requiring users to provide additional verification during login.

6. Security controls implemented:
   - The UI Service implements several security controls, including:
     - Secure communication using HTTPS to encrypt data in transit.
     - Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) and Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF) protection to prevent common web vulnerabilities.
     - Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) to ensure users have appropriate permissions for their roles.
     - Regular security testing and code reviews to identify and mitigate potential vulnerabilities.
     - Compliance with PCI DSS, RBI Guidelines, and ISO/IEC 27001 to ensure adherence to industry standards and regulations.

It also ensures compliance with PCI DSS and GDPR regulations by not storing sensitive information and providing secure access controls.

1. Primary functionality and purpose:

# Introduction

NextBank is a microservices-based digital banking platform designed to offer customers a secure and seamless online banking experience, enabling personal account management, fund transfers, and transaction history access while providing bank staff with robust administrative controls and reporting tools.

# Functional Flows

1. User Registration and Login: Customers can register and log in to access their accounts. The process involves the UI capturing user details, which are then sent to the API Gateway. The Auth Service validates the credentials and issues a token for session management.

2. Account Creation and Overview: Customers can create new accounts and view existing account details. The UI sends requests to the API Gateway, which routes them to the Account Service. The service manages account data and retrieves information from the database for display.

3. Fund Transfer: Customers initiate fund transfers via the UI. The request is routed through the API Gateway to the Auth Service for token validation. The Transaction Service checks the balance and recipient details before executing the transfer. The transaction is logged in the database, and the Notification Service sends a confirmation to the user.

4. Transaction History and Download: Customers can view and download their transaction history. The UI requests transaction data through the API Gateway, which is processed by the Transaction Service. The service retrieves the data from the database and formats it for download.

5. Notifications (SMS/Email/Push): Notifications are sent to users for various activities. The Notification Service interfaces with external systems like the SMS Gateway and Email Service to deliver messages based on user preferences.

6. Customer Support Ticketing: Customers can submit support tickets via the UI. The Ticketing Service manages ticket creation and updates, storing them in the database. Support staff can view and manage these tickets through the admin dashboard.

7. Admin Dashboard with User and Transaction Management: Administrators access a dashboard to manage users and transactions. The UI interacts with the User Management and Transaction Services via the API Gateway to perform CRUD operations and generate reports.

8. Reporting and Audit Tools: Administrators generate reports on transactions and user activities. The Reporting Service aggregates data from various services and formats it for compliance and analysis. The Audit Service logs all significant actions for security and compliance purposes.

# Third Party Integrations

1. Name of the third-party service: RBI Payment Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: Interbank transfer routing
   - Type of integration: REST APIs
   - Authentication method used: Auth
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction details for interbank transfers

2. Name of the third-party service: SMS Gateway
   - Purpose of integration: User notification
   - Type of integration: HTTP-based API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User phone numbers and notification messages

3. Name of the third-party service: Email Service (e.g., SES)
   - Purpose of integration: Email notifications
   - Type of integration: SMTP & API
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: User email addresses and notification content

4. Name of the third-party service: KYC Provider
   - Purpose of integration: Identity verification
   - Type of integration: OAuth-API
   - Authentication method used: OAuth
   - Data shared with the third party: User identity information for verification

5. Name of the third-party service: Fraud Detection Engine
   - Purpose of integration: Transaction anomaly checks
   - Type of integration: Kafka topic integration
   - Authentication method used: Not specified
   - Data shared with the third party: Transaction data for anomaly detection

# Introduction
